style="text-align: left;">Source: Czech <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Information_Publication" title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a> at the Air Navigation Services of the Czech Republic (ANS CR)<sup id="cite_ref-AIP_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>V\xc3\xa1clav Havel Airport Prague</b> (<a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <i lang="cs">Leti\xc5\xa1t\xc4\x9b V\xc3\xa1clava Havla Praha</i>), formerly <i>Prague Ruzyn\xc4\x9b International Airport</i> (<a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <i lang="cs">Mezin\xc3\xa1rodn\xc3\xad leti\xc5\xa1t\xc4\x9b Praha-Ruzyn\xc4\x9b</i>, <small>Czech pronunciation:&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Czech" title="Help:IPA/Czech">[\xcb\x88pra\xc9\xa6a \xcb\x88ruz\xc9\xaa\xc9\xb2\xc9\x9b]</a></span>) (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>PRG</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>LKPR</b>), is the <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> of <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>. The airport was founded in 1937, when it replaced the <a href="/wiki/Prague%E2%80%93Kbely_Airport" title="Prague\xe2\x80\x93Kbely Airport">Kbely Airport</a> (founded in 1918). It was reconstructed and extended in 1956, 1968, 1997, and 2006. In 2012, it was renamed after the last president of <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> and the first president of the Czech Republic, <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Havel" title="V\xc3\xa1clav Havel">V\xc3\xa1clav Havel</a>. It is located at the edge of the Prague-<a href="/wiki/Ruzyn%C4%9B" title="Ruzyn\xc4\x9b">Ruzyn\xc4\x9b</a> area, next to <a href="/wiki/Kn%C4%9B%C5%BEeves_(Prague-West_District)" title="Kn\xc4\x9b\xc5\xbeeves (Prague-West District)">Kn\xc4\x9b\xc5\xbeeves</a> village, 12&#160;km (7&#160;mi) west of the centre of <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a><sup id="cite_ref-AIP_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and 12&#160;km (7&#160;mi) southeast of the city of <a href="/wiki/Kladno" title="Kladno">Kladno</a>.\n</p><p>In 2018 it served around 17 million passengers<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> (expecting 18 million in 2019). It serves as a hub for <a href="/wiki/Czech_Airlines" title="Czech Airlines">Czech Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smartwings" title="Smartwings">Smartwings</a>, and as a base for <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruzyn%C4%9B,_star%C3%A9_leti%C5%A1t%C4%9B_(04).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Ruzyn%C4%9B%2C_star%C3%A9_leti%C5%A1t%C4%9B_%2804%29.jpg/220px-Ruzyn%C4%9B%2C_star%C3%A9_leti%C5%A1t%C4%9B_%2804%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Ruzyn%C4%9B%2C_star%C3%A9_leti%C5%A1t%C4%9B_%2804%29.jpg/330px-Ruzyn%C4%9B%2C_star%C3%A9_leti%C5%A1t%C4%9B_%2804%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Ruzyn%C4%9B%2C_star%C3%A9_leti%C5%A1t%C4%9B_%2804%29.jpg/440px-Ruzyn%C4%9B%2C_star%C3%A9_leti%C5%A1t%C4%9B_%2804%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5090" data-file-height="3753" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruzyn%C4%9B,_star%C3%A9_leti%C5%A1t%C4%9B_(04).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Old control tower built in 1937 (rear view) \xe2\x80\x93 now part of Terminal 4</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eisenhower_at_Prague_Airport_1945.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Eisenhower_at_Prague_Airport_1945.jpg/220px-Eisenhower_at_Prague_Airport_1945.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Eisenhower_at_Prague_Airport_1945.jpg/330px-Eisenhower_at_Prague_Airport_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Eisenhower_at_Prague_Airport_1945.jpg/440px-Eisenhower_at_Prague_Airport_1945.jpg 2x" data-file-width="834" data-file-height="585" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eisenhower_at_Prague_Airport_1945.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Old control tower (front view) during the visit of <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> to Prague on 12 October 1945</div></div></div>\n<p>Prague\xe2\x80\x93Ruzyn\xc4\x9b Airport began operations on 5 April 1937,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> but Czechoslovak civil aviation history started at the military airport in Prague\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Kbely" class="mw-redirect" title="Kbely">Kbely</a> in 1919. The <a href="/wiki/Prague_Aviation_Museum,_Kbely" class="mw-redirect" title="Prague Aviation Museum, Kbely">Prague Aviation Museum</a> is now found at Kbely Airport.\n</p><p>Due to insufficient capacity of Kbely Airport by the mid-1930s, the government decided to develop a new state civil airport in Ruzyn\xc4\x9b.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> One of the major awards Prague Ruzyn\xc4\x9b Airport received include Diploma and Gold Medal granted in 1937 at the occasion of the <a href="/wiki/Exposition_Internationale_des_Arts_et_Techniques_dans_la_Vie_Moderne" title="Exposition Internationale des Arts et Techniques dans la Vie Moderne">International Art and Technical Exhibition in Paris</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> (<i>Exposition Internationale des Arts et Techniques dans la Vie Moderne</i> also known as <i>Paris 1937 World\'s Fair</i>) for the technical conception of the central airport, primarily the architecture of the check-in building (nowadays known as Terminal 4) designed by architect Adolf Ben\xc5\xa1.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In one of the most dramatic moments in its history, the airport was seized by Soviet paratroopers on the night of 20\xe2\x80\x9321 August 1968, who then facilitated the landing of Soviet troops and transports for the invasion of Czechoslovakia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Moreover, the Ruzyn\xc4\x9b fields provide opportunities for further expansion of the airport according to the increasing capacity demand. The airport serves as a hub of the trans-European airport network.\n</p><p>The political and economic changes affected the seventy years of existence of Prague\xe2\x80\x93Ruzyn\xc4\x9b Airport. Some new air transportation companies and institutions were founded and some ceased operation since then. Ten entities have been responsible for airport administration over time, including the new construction and development. Until the 1990s, there were two or three-decade gaps before the major modernisation of Prague\xe2\x80\x93Ruzyn\xc4\x9b Airport began to match the current capacity requirements.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The airport stood in for <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami International Airport</a> in the 2006 <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_in_film" class="mw-redirect" title="James Bond in film">James Bond</a> film <a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(2006_film)" title="Casino Royale (2006 film)">Casino Royale</a>.\n</p><p>An online petition organised by one of the best-known Slovak film directors, Fero Feni\xc4\x8d, calling on the government and the Parliament to rename Prague Ruzyn\xc4\x9b Airport to <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Havel" title="V\xc3\xa1clav Havel">V\xc3\xa1clav Havel</a> International Airport attracted \xe2\x80\x93 in just one week after 20 December 2011 \xe2\x80\x93 the support of over 65,000 signatories both within and outside the Czech Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> A rendition of the airport with the proposed <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Havel" title="V\xc3\xa1clav Havel">V\xc3\xa1clav Havel</a> name in the form of his signature followed by his typical heart symbol suffix was included in the blog\'s article in support of renaming of the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> This name change took place on 5 October 2012 on what would have been Havel\'s 76th birthday. However, the PRG name of the airport for IATA and ICAO will remain the same.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_development">Further development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Further development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_one_the_Prague_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/View_one_the_Prague_Airport.jpg/220px-View_one_the_Prague_Airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/View_one_the_Prague_Airport.jpg/330px-View_one_the_Prague_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/View_one_the_Prague_Airport.jpg/440px-View_one_the_Prague_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5462" data-file-height="3072" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_one_the_Prague_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View on pier B (Terminal 1) and C (Terminal 2)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_Airport_Terminal_1_-_Arrivals.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Prague_Airport_Terminal_1_-_Arrivals.jpg/220px-Prague_Airport_Terminal_1_-_Arrivals.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Prague_Airport_Terminal_1_-_Arrivals.jpg/330px-Prague_Airport_Terminal_1_-_Arrivals.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Prague_Airport_Terminal_1_-_Arrivals.jpg/440px-Prague_Airport_Terminal_1_-_Arrivals.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_Airport_Terminal_1_-_Arrivals.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 1 of Prague Airport</div></div></div>\n<p>As the capacity of the airport has been reaching its limit for the last couple of years (as of 2005),<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> further development of the airport is being considered. Besides regular repairs of the existing runways, Prague Airport (<a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <i lang="cs">Leti\xc5\xa1t\xc4\x9b Praha s.p.</i>) began the preparations for building a new runway, parallel to the 06/24 runway. The construction with estimated costs of <a href="/wiki/Czech_koruna" title="Czech koruna">CZK</a> 5\xe2\x80\x937&#160;billion was scheduled to begin in 2007, and the new runway marked 06R/24L (also called the BIS runway) was to be put into service in 2010. However, because of many legal problems and the protests of people who live close to the airport premises, the construction has not yet begun. Despite these problems, the project has support from the government, and is expected to be completed by the end of 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It will be over 3,500&#160;m (11,483&#160;ft) long. Located about 1,500&#160;m (4,921&#160;ft) southeast of the present main runway, the 24L runway will be equipped with a category III <a href="/wiki/Instrument_Landing_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Instrument Landing System">ILS</a>, allowing landing and taking off under bad weather conditions.\n</p><p>Prague Airport states that besides increasing the airport capacity, the new runway system will greatly reduce the noise level in some densely inhabited areas of Prague. This should be achieved by reorganising the air traffic space around the airport, and shifting the traffic corridors after putting the two parallel runways into service. The vision of heavy traffic raised many protests from the suburban communities directly surrounding the airport. On 6 November 2004, local <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referenda</a> were held in two Prague suburbs \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Nebu%C5%A1ice" title="Nebu\xc5\xa1ice">Nebu\xc5\xa1ice</a> and <a href="/wiki/P%C5%99edn%C3%AD_Kopanina" title="P\xc5\x99edn\xc3\xad Kopanina">P\xc5\x99edn\xc3\xad Kopanina</a> \xe2\x80\x93 giving official support to the local authorities for active opposition against the construction of the parallel runway.\n</p><p>The construction of a railway connection between the airport and Prague city centre is also in the planning stage. The track will be served by express trains with special fares, connecting non-stop the airport with the city centre, and local trains fully integrated into Prague integrated transit system.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_runway_reconstruction">General runway reconstruction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: General runway reconstruction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The main runway 06/24 was reconstructed from 2012 - 2013 due to poor technical conditions. During reconstruction, runway 12/30 was the only usable runway as runway 04/22 is closed permanently.<sup id="cite_ref-closed_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-closed-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The runway reconstruction was originally planned for three stages. The first stage in 2012, the second stage in 2013 and the last stage in 2014. However, runway 12/30 (which would be used during the reconstruction of the main runway) is not equipped for low visibility landings as it offers only <a href="/wiki/Instrument_landing_system" title="Instrument landing system">ILS</a> CAT I landings. In addition, the approach path of runway 12/30 goes above high-density population areas (such as <a href="/wiki/Prague_6" title="Prague 6">Prague 6</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kladno" title="Kladno">Kladno</a>). Therefore, the second and the third stage of the runway reconstruction had to be merged so the works could be finished in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PRG_Airport_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/PRG_Airport_Map.png/220px-PRG_Airport_Map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/PRG_Airport_Map.png/330px-PRG_Airport_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/PRG_Airport_Map.png/440px-PRG_Airport_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="2800" data-file-height="1970" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PRG_Airport_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Airport Map</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_Airport_Terminal_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Prague_Airport_Terminal_2.jpg/220px-Prague_Airport_Terminal_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Prague_Airport_Terminal_2.jpg/330px-Prague_Airport_Terminal_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Prague_Airport_Terminal_2.jpg/440px-Prague_Airport_Terminal_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_Airport_Terminal_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 2 of Prague Airport</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Prague Airport has two main passenger terminals, two general aviation terminals, as well as a cargo facility. Most flights depart Prague Airport from the North Terminals (Terminal 1 and 2). The South Terminals (Terminal 3 and 4) handle a few irregular flights, as well as VIP flights, special flights and small aircraft.\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Terminal 1</b> is used for flights outside the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>; it was opened in 1968 and rebuilt in 1997, it includes concourses A and B</li>\n<li><b>Terminal 2</b> is used for flights within the Schengen area; it was opened on 17 January 2006, it includes concourses C and D</li>\n<li><b>Terminal 3</b> is used for private and charter flights; it was opened in 1997</li>\n<li><b>Terminal 4</b> is used exclusively for VIP flights and state visits; it is the oldest part of the airport which was opened on 5 April 1937.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>There are also two freight terminals, <i>Cargo Terminal 1</i> is operated by Menzies Aviation Czech while <i>Cargo Terminal 2</i> is operated by Skyport.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Runways">Runways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Runways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport contains two <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runways</a> in service: 06/24 (till April 1993 07/25) and 12/30 (till May 2012 13/31). Former runway 04/22 is permanently closed for take-offs and landings and is used for taxiing and parking only.<sup id="cite_ref-AIP_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-closed_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-closed-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The most used runway is 24 due to the prevailing western winds. Runway 30 is also used often. Runway 06 is used rarely, while runway 12 is used only exceptionally.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The company operating the airport is Prague Airport (<i>Leti\xc5\xa1t\xc4\x9b Praha, a. s.</i>), a <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company" title="Joint-stock company">joint-stock company</a> that has one shareholder, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Finance_(Czech_Republic)" title="Ministry of Finance (Czech Republic)">Ministry of Finance</a>. The company was founded in February 2008, as part of a privatisation process involving the Airport Prague (<i>Spr\xc3\xa1va Leti\xc5\xa1t\xc4\x9b Praha, s.p.</i>) state enterprise. This action was in accordance with the Czech Republic Government Memorandum Nr. 888, which had been passed on 9 July 2008. On 1 December 2008, Prague Airport took all rights and duties formerly held by Spr\xc3\xa1va Leti\xc5\xa1t\xc4\x9b Praha, s.p., and Prague Airports took all business authorisations, certificates, employees, and licenses from the former company.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The head office of Prague Airport is in <a href="/wiki/Prague_6" title="Prague 6">Prague 6</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The former state-owned enterprise had its head office on the airport property.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="500" /></a></span> Spain</td>\n<td>726,301\n</td>\n<td>1,091,450\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_facilities">Other facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Other facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CSA_building_Ruzyne.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/CSA_building_Ruzyne.jpg/220px-CSA_building_Ruzyne.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/CSA_building_Ruzyne.jpg/330px-CSA_building_Ruzyne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/CSA_building_Ruzyne.jpg/440px-CSA_building_Ruzyne.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="2400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CSA_building_Ruzyne.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>APC Building, the head office of <a href="/wiki/Czech_Airlines" title="Czech Airlines">Czech Airlines</a> at Prague Airport</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Czech_Airlines" title="Czech Airlines">Czech Airlines</a> has its head office, the APC Building,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> on the grounds of Prague Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> On 30 December 2009 CSA announced that it will sell its head office to the airport for CZK 607&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Smartwings" title="Smartwings">Smartwings</a> have their head office on the airport property.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In addition the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(Czech_Republic)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (Czech Republic)">Civil Aviation Authority</a> also has its head office on the airport property.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transportation">Ground transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ground transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Buses_in_Prague" title="Buses in Prague">Buses of DPP</a>, the Prague Public Transit Co., stop at both terminals 1 and 2 frequently. A <a href="/wiki/Czech_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Czech Railways">Czech Railways</a> public bus service, AE \xe2\x80\x93 AirportExpress, connects Terminal 1 with <a href="/wiki/Praha_hlavn%C3%AD_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD" title="Praha hlavn\xc3\xad n\xc3\xa1dra\xc5\xbe\xc3\xad">Praha hlavn\xc3\xad n\xc3\xa1dra\xc5\xbe\xc3\xad</a>. From bus station in front of Terminal 1 there are also regular buses to <a href="/wiki/Kladno" title="Kladno">Kladno</a>, intercity buses of <a href="/wiki/Student_Agency" title="Student Agency">Regiojet</a> run every 30\xe2\x80\x9360 minutes to <a href="/wiki/Karlovy_Vary" title="Karlovy Vary">Karlovy Vary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cheb" title="Cheb">Cheb</a>.\n</p><p>There are plans to build a rail connection to the airport. Preliminary work commenced in 2018, with procurement proceedings launched the following year. Main construction is likely to start around 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>On 19 February 1973, <a href="/wiki/Aeroflot_Flight_141_(1973)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aeroflot Flight 141 (1973)">Aeroflot Flight 141</a>, during <a href="/wiki/Final_approach_(aeronautics)" title="Final approach (aeronautics)">approach</a> a <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-154" title="Tupolev Tu-154">Tupolev Tu-154</a> crashed half a kilometre short of the airport. While most of the passengers survived the crash many died in the fire that followed. Altogether 66 people died from the 100 passengers and crew. The crash was the first loss of and the first fatal accident involving a Tu-154.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 30 October 1975, <a href="/wiki/Inex-Adria_Aviopromet_Flight_450" title="Inex-Adria Aviopromet Flight 450">Inex-Adria Aviopromet Flight 450</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-9-32" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas DC-9-32">Douglas DC-9-32</a> hit high ground during an approach in fog to Prague Ruzyn\xc4\x9b Airport. 75 of the 120 passengers and crew on board were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 29 March 1989, two teenagers from <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> armed with grenades and shotguns hijacked <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9v_Hungarian_Airlines" title="Mal\xc3\xa9v Hungarian Airlines">Mal\xc3\xa9v</a> Flight 640 at Prague Ruzyn\xc4\x9b Airport, and forced the <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-154B" class="mw-redirect" title="Tupolev Tu-154B">Tupolev Tu-154B</a> with 15 hostages to fly to <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> before surrendering.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a
